    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6629846395211270631">Tal como afirma el propio J.J. Benitez, "adelantar el argumento y la naturaleza de Caballo de Troya es quebrar el desconcertante misterio que encierran sus páginas". Podemos apuntar, eso sí, que para la elaboración de esta obra el autor se ha basado en una documentación real, depositada hace años en Estados Unidos. Una documentación que pone al descubierto multitud de dato</span>
  <span id="freeText6629846395211270631" style="display:none">Tal como afirma el propio J.J. Benitez, "adelantar el argumento y la naturaleza de Caballo de Troya es quebrar el desconcertante misterio que encierran sus páginas". Podemos apuntar, eso sí, que para la elaboración de esta obra el autor se ha basado en una documentación real, depositada hace años en Estados Unidos. Una documentación que pone al descubierto multitud de datos nuevos sobre la figura y obra de Jesús de Nazaret. Podemos asegurar que -tal y como sospecha buena parte de la Humanidad- las grandes potencias ocultan muchos de sus proyectos espaciales y militares, y "Caballo de Troya" es una prueba más de ello.<br />Podemos revelar, por ejemplo, que en 1973 las fuerzas aéreas norteamericanas, después de varios años de preparación y tras un sinfín de peripecias, ejecutaron en pleno corazón de Israel uno de sus proyectos "supersecretos" que fue bautizado, precisamente, como "Operación Caballo de Troya". Pero no podemos avanzar al lector cómo se consiguió esa fascinante documentación "confidencial" por parte de J.J. Benitez, ni tampoco el asombroso desarrollo de la referida operación y su desconcertante final. Sería romper el encanto de Caballo de Troya, primer libro testimonio del periodista y escritor navarro...En palabras del autor: "...será el futuro, como sucedió con Julio Verne, quien pondrá de manifiesto si este relato fue o no verídico".</span>
  <a data-text-id="6629846395211270631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {

  <span id="freeText18304156638811716101" style="display:none">The message on this book is AMAZING, it's like watching and listening to Jesus in real time, his thoughts, conversations and personality are reflected in the book in ways that I never even thought could be possible. We always think of Jesus as a our savior, but almost never think of him as the amazing human being he was. On the other side, reading 1200 pages for a journey that is only 3 days long could be tedious. Details are not a few paragraphs but pages and pages, and sometimes way too graphic, medical and technical. It said a couple of retarded things like Jesus had blood brothers and sisters, which is something that it's not true, that was the only part that annoyed me a little, but the message on the book left me praying and thanking Jesus for dying to save us from our sins, and God for sending his son to this world to evangelize his word. </span>

They are fascinating to read.<br/><br/>The author writes them as a non-fiction account of a supposed NASA Time traveler's memoirs (think Da Vinci Code). <br/><br/>According to the book the time traveler wrote his memoirs and stashed them away, but they were found by Benitez and published as Caballo de Troya (Trojan Horse, which is the name of the time machine).   <span id="freeText6132854286883042000" style="display:none">I don't think these have been translated to English yet, but they should. They are fascinating to read.<br /><br />The author writes them as a non-fiction account of a supposed NASA Time traveler's memoirs (think Da Vinci Code). <br /><br />According to the book the time traveler wrote his memoirs and stashed them away, but they were found by Benitez and published as Caballo de Troya (Trojan Horse, which is the name of the time machine). What makes it a great read is that they visit Jerusalem around the time of Jesus' ministry and actually become his disciples for two years. <br /><br />I liked how he fleshed out more of the details of what it would be like to have followed Jesus through his years traveling the countryside preaching and then his trials and tribulations in the final months of his life.<br /><br />Very well written and entertaining. Keep an eye out for them in English. </span>

    <a title="Yvette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5925807-yvette"><img alt="Yvette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594928433p2/5925807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3160737219?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yvette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yvette" href="/user/show/5925807-yvette">Yvette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5925807-yvette?shelf=books-i-ve-read-in-2020">books-i-ve-read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3160737219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13688784057385632085">Loved this book. Definitely not everyone's cup of tea. It could be excessively descriptive, but I think at least, that the more details we get particularly for this book the better context we have to properly understand it. I tried reading it with a very open skeptical mind, but I admit I found myself crying so many times. At least for me, is the message was mind blowing, I kept thinking about it often during my day. Fiction or not, this book left me with a positive message and a new way to see </span>
  <span id="freeText13688784057385632085" style="display:none">Loved this book. Definitely not everyone's cup of tea. It could be excessively descriptive, but I think at least, that the more details we get particularly for this book the better context we have to properly understand it. I tried reading it with a very open skeptical mind, but I admit I found myself crying so many times. At least for me, is the message was mind blowing, I kept thinking about it often during my day. Fiction or not, this book left me with a positive message and a new way to see life. The fact that Jesus Christ was portrayed wrongly (no surprise) throughout the bible (as we know it) made me doubt of the current interpretations. When we see Jesus Christ as a human overall, it all makes more sense. <br /><br />The footnotes at the end, I agree, were excessive, and perhaps unnecessary (not all of them). I don't think I will read the following books yet. I am afraid I will be disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13688784057385632085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2750758305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2750758305" />
    <a title="Luan Carlesso" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/94698492-luan-carlesso"><img alt="Luan Carlesso" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554134041p2/94698492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2750758305?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luan Carlesso" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luan Carlesso" href="/user/show/94698492-luan-carlesso">Luan Carlesso</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9788576653738" href="/book/show/22024079-jerusal-m">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2750758305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5568421099134392286">The story from Jesus is well known by every Christian (and other people as well) in the world, but the job that Benítez had done is incredibly well detailed and described. It seems that a lot of research was needed to get this book write and the result, as consequence, was an amazing ficcion. It's inclusively hard to say whats real of creation. The story is about a cientist that, favored by a futuristic technology, was able to travel to the past, just a few days before Jesus crucification. His m</span>
  <span id="freeText5568421099134392286" style="display:none">The story from Jesus is well known by every Christian (and other people as well) in the world, but the job that Benítez had done is incredibly well detailed and described. It seems that a lot of research was needed to get this book write and the result, as consequence, was an amazing ficcion. It's inclusively hard to say whats real of creation. The story is about a cientist that, favored by a futuristic technology, was able to travel to the past, just a few days before Jesus crucification. His mission is to follow all the events from the day of his arrival until the ressurection of Jesus, reporting it to "Trojan Horse Project". So, he describes every event, conversation and result of his investigation in a manner to documentate and compare the real events to the ones described at the bible. For that, he is in own of some futuristic devices as well, that possibilitate deep analysis of a lot of factors and variables, as chemical composition of some substances, or even Jesus health, for example.<br />After reading it, i was in a mix of feelings. Firstly, i was very intrigued and envolved in the story. It's very interesting to think about how Jesus fascinated and moved crowds, resulting in what we witness nowadays, and even harder to imagine all the possible things suffered by him and, despite of that, to keep with his determination and faith in his goal. But, it was very hard to read this book without thinking in jump some pages. Benítez overstates about the technological devices explanation and facts about the story, making crucial events very exhausting to read. The crucification, for example, an event that seems to had lasted just an hour, looks like a whole day in the book. If he hasn't attached too much to the details, the book would be smaller and more entertaining. The reader woudn't be tired and desmotivated so frequently. Because of these low points, i'm really reconsidering if i have the enough energy to read the remaining 8 books of the series. Anyway, it's a very good read and had worth it. If you are not easily discouraged by long and exhausting books, you'll enjoy it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5568421099134392286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_849213502" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/849213502" />
    <a title="Robson Castilho" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9324950-robson-castilho"><img alt="Robson Castilho" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559183207p2/9324950.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/849213502?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robson Castilho" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robson Castilho" href="/user/show/9324950-robson-castilho">Robson Castilho</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9788576653738" href="/book/show/22024079-jerusal-m">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9324950-robson-castilho?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer849213502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11162006098431696644">As a big fan of "time travelling", I began reading this book with positive expectations.<br/><br/>However, as the pages went by, my excitement gave way to boredom. Narrated as the daily of the US Major who made the trip, the book is annoyingly full of details, keeping the story stuck through numerous pages while explaining about vegetation, clothing, food, currency, etc. Excessive detail is even bigger in science and anatomy, which makes the book difficult to understand (unless you're a scientist or a doc</span>
  <span id="freeText11162006098431696644" style="display:none">As a big fan of "time travelling", I began reading this book with positive expectations.<br /><br />However, as the pages went by, my excitement gave way to boredom. Narrated as the daily of the US Major who made the trip, the book is annoyingly full of details, keeping the story stuck through numerous pages while explaining about vegetation, clothing, food, currency, etc. Excessive detail is even bigger in science and anatomy, which makes the book difficult to understand (unless you're a scientist or a doctor).<br /><br />Conversations with Jesus are the best parts of the book but ended up buried in the midst of so many details.<br /><br />Another point that bothers a bit is the extreme ease with which the Major manage to "infiltrate" among Jesus' followers, earning everyone's trust and getting to be in almost every major event without any complication.<br /><br />For all that, I will not read the rest of the series - whose books are bigger than this one - and if you don't like overly-detailed books, you may also not like this series.<br />---------------------------------------------<br /><br />Portuguese version:<br /><br />Eu, como grande fã do tema "viagem no tempo", comecei a ler este livro com bastante expectativa. <br />No entanto, a medida que as páginas iam passando, minha animação foi dando lugar ao tédio. Narrado como um diário do major que fez a viagem, o livro é irritantemente detalhista, mantendo a história emperrada por inúmeras páginas enquanto explica sobre vegetação, vestuário, alimentação, moedas da época, etc.<br />O excesso de detalhes é ainda maior em questões científicas e de anatomia, o que torna o livro, em vários momentos, de difícil compreensão (a menos que você seja cientista ou um médico).<br />As conversas com Jesus são as melhores partes do livro mas acabaram ficando soterradas no meio de tantos detalhes.<br />Outro ponto que incomoda um pouco é a extrema facilidade com que o major consegue se "infiltrar" entre os seguidores de Jesus, ganhando tranquilamente a confiança de todos e conseguindo estar em todos os eventos importantes quase sem nenhuma complicação.<br />Por tudo isso, não lerei o restante da série - cujos livros são ainda maiores - e se você não gosta de livros muito arrastados, que focam mais no cenário do que na história, é possível que também não goste desta série.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11162006098431696644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+0U9O76N5GXHq66vQM/XXNRgssOqG6OwQVVWnwC8kDiKQ2VSeR8GAWcJYmTbZv49eJ4ckRBaE78CE+rdJw5kHQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QeO05pXtT1k6TU4R3lMNWFSXCZkJGRWAYuBlWY7fqaAw5eyPUn+tPZrvgtpF+iQ5+Gmny7NYpY8hptkbqW1dhQ==')})
  }

Juventud en éxtasis, enfrenta el tema del noviazgo y la elección de pareja en forma directa y actual proporcionando a los jóvenes armas para tomar las mejores decisiones. Esta es una obra literaria digna de análisis. Ha sido propuesta como lectura complementaria en miles de colegios de nivel medio y medio superior en todo el mundo de habla hispana.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"16289111469049292051\" href=\"#\" Salvar el fuego retrata dos Méxicos completamente escindidos uno del otro, donde Marina, que pertenece a la clase social más alta, se vincula con un hombre al extremo de la sociedad. Esta es una novela que retrata las contradicciones de un país y las contradicciones más hondas de la naturaleza humana. Es una novela de amor y es una novela que al final termina por brindar esperanza. «Una novela polifónica que narra con intensidad y con excepcional dinamismo una historia de violencia en el México contemporáneo donde el amor y la redención aún son posibles. El autor se sirve tantode una extraordinaria fuerza visual como de la recreación y reinvención del lenguaje coloquial para lograr una obra de inquietante verosimilitud. Los distintos planos narrativos tienen como hilo conductor el cuerpo humano, motivo de celebración y expuesto a numerosos excesos.»Del acta del jurado La crítica ha dicho:«El mexicano Guillermo Arriaga no es solo un escritor de la gran pantalla sino un narrador de raza, cuyas obsesiones vitales dejan honda huella en el lector.»Matías Néspolo, El Mundo «Un autor absolutamente único.»Guadalupe Nettel «Uno de los autores contemporáneos más potentes, intensos y originales de la literatura en idioma español.»El Exprés (México) «Arriaga demuestra ser gran director a la par que gran escritor.»Roberto Piorno, Guía del Ocio «Con sensibilidad extrema y poderío visual, enlazando con coherencia personajes y situaciones que inicialmente parecen no guardar relación [...], Arriaga demuestra que, además de un espléndido guionista, también es un buen director.»Carlos Boyero, El País «El Salvaje es uno de los mejores libros que he leído, no solo en este sino en los últimos años.»Santiago Gamboa «La presencia ominosa de la muerte; el amor o la pasión que todo lo crea y, por encima, la fuerza irrefrenable de la vida que arrastra todo consigo en su prepotencia arrolladora. Esos son los motivos que entrelaza con sabiduría en El Salvaje, una ambiciosa y lograda novela.»Matías Néspolo, El Mundo «Sublime Arriaga. El Salvaje consagra a su autor como el mejor escritor mexicano actual y como una figura indiscutible de las letras universales. [...] No os lo penséis y leedlo: vuestro espíritu os lo agradeceráGabri Ródenas, Zenda Libros «Su novela más ambiciosa y extensa, de estructura compleja e impregnada de elementos personales, en la que su personaje, Juan Guillermo, pese a las más terribles pérdidas, es capaz de reconstruir su vida.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"6786335461866821704\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9116174995332675739">The works of J. J. Benítez encompass literature and journalism, as well as UFO investigations.Primarily renowned as an investigator of the paranormal, Benítez garnered attention and criticism when he released Jerusalén, the first volume of a series named Caballo de Troya, related to the life and death of Jesus Christ. He begun his journalist career in January 1966 in the newspaper La Verdad, after</span>
  <span id="freeText9116174995332675739" style="display:none">The works of J. J. Benítez encompass literature and journalism, as well as UFO investigations.Primarily renowned as an investigator of the paranormal, Benítez garnered attention and criticism when he released Jerusalén, the first volume of a series named Caballo de Troya, related to the life and death of Jesus Christ. He begun his journalist career in January 1966 in the newspaper La Verdad, after receiving a journalism degree from the University of Navarra in 1965. He published his first books in 1975, Ovni: S.O.S a la Humanidad and Existió Otra Humanidad.<br /><br />During his three decades as an author, he has published more than 50 books, including investigative reports, essays, novels and poetry, and sold more than nine million copies worldwide. As of May 2007, 7 million copies has been sold from the first 8 books of the Caballo de Troya series. He has also directed a TV documentary series called Planeta Encantado, in which he travels to 17 different countries in order to render his interpretation of some of the great unsolved mysteries of past history.</span>

Hijo del Hombre aparece de nuevo, fascinando con sus palabras y su irresistible humanidad.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"214082333439786425\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return
